## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (continuous-time growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt, the instantaneous population growth rate as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics. Common relationships encode per-capita growth dependence on density (P) and external forcing or interventions through time (t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Affine per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (trend in growth conditions over time)
- Verhulst-type density dependence (quadratic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (crowding/carrying-capacity effect with c1 ~ 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (Richards differential form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) ** c2 (flexible approach to saturation via shape parameter)
- Gompertz ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases logarithmically with size)
- Generalized Gompertz with time-varying rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P * log(c3 / P) (changing environment affects Gompertz rate)
- Ricker-type continuous inhibition: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong density suppression via exponential factor)
- Allee-effect (strong Allee) cubic form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below a threshold and negative above carrying capacity)
- Beverton–Holt–like saturating recruitment with linear loss: dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (recruitment saturates; mortality proportional to P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (removal independent of P, e.g., quotas)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to population size)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment modulates intrinsic growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P across the data range, the governing law is likely density-independent (linear-in-P) growth with a possibly time-varying coefficient.
- If dP_dt becomes negative at high P and the dP_dt vs P curve is concave downward with a single peak, a quadratic-in-P suppression term (P - P^2 pattern) is typical of carrying-capacity limitation.
- If the per-capita growth dP_dt / P decreases roughly linearly with P, use polynomial density dependence (e.g., 1 - c*P); if it decreases nonlinearly, prefer exponentiated or power-shaped terms like exp(-c*P) or (1 - c*P)^k.
- If dP_dt / P appears linear in log(P), a log term (Gompertz-type) is indicated because log(c/P) produces linear structure in log(P).
- If growth is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P (a low-density threshold), include an Allee factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying the rest of the dynamics.
- If dP_dt shows periodic sign or amplitude modulation over time at similar P, include sinusoidal forcing in t multiplying P (environmental seasonality).
- If dP_dt is systematically shifted downward by an approximately constant amount across P, add a constant subtraction term (constant-yield harvesting or stocking/removal offset).
- If dP_dt crosses zero at nearly the same P regardless of t, the equilibrium is primarily density-set (P-driven); if the zero-crossing shifts with t, consider explicit t-dependence in growth or carrying-capacity terms.
- If dP_dt increases with P for small P but then saturates rather than turning over, use saturating recruitment terms like P/(P+c) with a separate mortality term.

1. `P` (linear term)
2. `P²` (quadratic term)
3. `P^(1/3)` (cube root term)
4. `P*exp(-c*t)` (exponential decay times P)

Let me first check if `P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2` can represent `aP + bP²`. 

`P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2 = c0*P/(P+c1) + c2*P`

Finding common denominator: `= (c0*P + c2*P*(P+c1))/(P+c1) = (c0*P + c2*P² + c2*c1*P)/(P+c1) = (c2*P² + (c0+c2*c1)*P)/(P+c1)`

For this to equal `aP + bP²`, we need: `c2*P² + (c0+c2*c1)*P = (aP + bP²)(P+c1) = bP³ + (a+bc1)P² + ac1*P`

This introduces a P³ term, so `P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2` CANNOT exactly equal `aP + bP²` (a polynomial). The rational function `P/(P+c1)` with c1≠0 is fundamentally different from a polynomial.

So candidates using `P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2` as their "polynomial" part cannot match GT unless they have additional terms that compensate.
